<div id="review_1678756038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1678756038" />
    <a title="Althea Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann"><img alt="Althea Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411566466p2/3846743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1678756038?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Althea Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Althea Ann" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann">Althea Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1678756038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12694197543712346935">Read as part of the Hugo Voters' Packet.<br/><br/>Enjoyable YA space adventure with an engaging protagonist. <br/>In this future, the Himba tribe of Namibia are an insular minority, looked down upon by the majority Khoush although the Himba have become specialized experts in math and 'harmonizing,' producing "astrolabes" (which seem to be the future's smartphones). Teenage Binti's skills have won her a coveted scholarship to an intergalactic university, but to her family, it is unthinkable that she would be pe</span>
  <span id="freeText12694197543712346935" style="display:none">Read as part of the Hugo Voters' Packet.<br /><br />Enjoyable YA space adventure with an engaging protagonist. <br />In this future, the Himba tribe of Namibia are an insular minority, looked down upon by the majority Khoush although the Himba have become specialized experts in math and 'harmonizing,' producing "astrolabes" (which seem to be the future's smartphones). Teenage Binti's skills have won her a coveted scholarship to an intergalactic university, but to her family, it is unthinkable that she would be permitted to leave her tribe and go. Unwilling to let her dreams die, Binti runs away and soon finds herself on a ship en route to Oomza Uni. Unfortunately, that ship is hijacked by alien terrorists.<br /><br />Although the setup is both fun and fascinating, there were a few plot holes and the way things eventually worked out was too easy and simplistic, I thought. <br /><br />My issues with the story:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <br />1. Most significantly, I'm not saying that it is impossible to become best buddies with the terrorist who murdered your crush, all your new friends and classmates, and well, EVERYONE on the ship you're traveling on. But if that's going to happen, it needs to be a lot more carefully done. The psychological complexity and ambiguity of the situation needs to be acknowledged, at the very least, and it isn't here, at all.<br /><br />2. On a related note, although yes, the professors at the Uni did both the right and the sensible thing by acceding to the terrorists' demands, it seems inconceivable that none of them would mention the slaughter of a boatload of their colleagues, some of whom would undoubtedly have been close friends, lovers, family... No grief or anger at their loss is shown - only a bit of anger at demands being made. Overall, the mass murder is treated like a quickly-forgotten no-big-deal.<br /><br />3. Binti's skin treatment is revealed to be a cure-all to the alien Meduse race. Luckily, it turns out that the formula is not unique to Namibia; it can be produced elsewhere. However, no mention at all is made of the immediately obvious situation: if something you have is valuable to a warlike species, you and ALL OF YOUR PEOPLE are in deep danger. It never seems to occur to Binti that if she can't provide more of it, the Meduse would undoubtedly invade Namibia for it.<br /><br />4. In a story this short, there's room for a limited number of unexplained and logically unlikely thingummies. We start out with one, the mysterious 'edan' that Binti found in the desert and uses as a good luck charm. It sure is convenient, when she's attacked, that her good luck charm turns out to be a mentally-powered force shield AND translation device! But, seeing as there wouldn't be much of a story if it wasn't, I can accept that. All the Meduse are appropriately shocked that she can suddenly communicate with them. However, that's kind of negated when later, it turns out that communication can ALSO be facilitated by a quick 'sting' that's actually some kind of DNA/blood transfusion... I think that having either the 'sting' or the 'edan' as a plot device, but not both, would've made the story stronger.<br /><br />5. As one last minor point, I would've liked more on what 'harmonizing' is and how a math/engineering-related skill translates into negotiation skills. But that's mostly just because Binti's professional thought processes are interesting. I wanted to find out more about the 'astrolabes' she makes, too!<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="12694197543712346935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2486662070" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2486662070" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2486662070?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2486662070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17842307655039608332"><i>
  <b>“No matter what choice I made, I was never going to have a normal life, really. I looked around and immediately knew what to do next.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Awards are not to be trusted.<br/><br/>Sometimes they get it right by accident, but for the most part the assessment criteria seem to have little to do with the quality of the work. <br/><br/><i>Binti</i> tells the story of the girl Binti (surprise!) of the Himba people, primitive isolationists who are desperately reluctant to hinder her, a prodigy among them, to leave their reclusive s</span>
  <span id="freeText17842307655039608332" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“No matter what choice I made, I was never going to have a normal life, really. I looked around and immediately knew what to do next.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Awards are not to be trusted.<br /><br />Sometimes they get it right by accident, but for the most part the assessment criteria seem to have little to do with the quality of the work. <br /><br /><i>Binti</i> tells the story of the girl Binti (surprise!) of the Himba people, primitive isolationists who are desperately reluctant to hinder her, a prodigy among them, to leave their reclusive society in order to attend space university. She does anyway, running away from her family, there are some extremely dangerous complications that she’s able to very easily solve because... she’s the protagonist, aaaand... the end.<br /><br /><i>Binti</i> is a novella not without its merits, but certainly not with any particular originality. Neither in the young protagonist from a disenfranchised primitive isolationist culture who's the first to partake in a prestigious institution. Nor in the exploration of culture clash between humans and aliens. These issues have been dealt with again and again by many works of fiction, often far more skilfully than in Binti. <br /><br />Then there is the juvenile writing style (which, admittedly, makes sense with the first person narrative of a teenage protagonist) and the deus ex machina and the plot holes defying all logic and rules of writing. Is this the mythical originality I've heard about, mayhap? <br /><br />At its core, Binti alternates between doing too much and too little, inevitably the curse of such a short novella. It can be read as a decent little story, that is neither thought-provoking nor intellectually stimulating, but for the right people (not me) I am sure can be quite fun. I personally thought it was boring and lazily written too, but that's just personal taste. However, I am not entirely uninterested in Okorafors work, and will be on the lookout for more of her writing in the future. Hopefully it proves a lot more of a positive experience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17842307655039608332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2217550843" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2217550843" />
    <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net"><img alt="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390032p2/7971097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2217550843?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net">Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25762847-binti">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2217550843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18073652204810763518">I expected more from this. There's some important themes about acceptance and colonialism addressed in here, for sure, but the execution is what I found most lacking. <br/><br/>As a novella, it works in that there's a clear beginning, middle and end. There's certainly plot movement as Binti leaves her homeland for an entirely new world and the prospect of education - an opportunity never given to the children of her people. The strongest part of the novel is certainly the beginning, as Binti's cultural he</span>
  <span id="freeText18073652204810763518" style="display:none">I expected more from this. There's some important themes about acceptance and colonialism addressed in here, for sure, but the execution is what I found most lacking. <br /><br />As a novella, it works in that there's a clear beginning, middle and end. There's certainly plot movement as Binti leaves her homeland for an entirely new world and the prospect of education - an opportunity never given to the children of her people. The strongest part of the novel is certainly the beginning, as Binti's cultural heritage and traditions were the aspect of the story I found the most compelling, and the most strongly developed. <br /><br />The rest of the story lacks the impact and finish I've come to look for in works of fiction that I end up loving. It doesn't help that I'm reading a really well-written novel right now, because in comparison the prose in this fell extremely flat. It's all too cut and dry telling, over showing. "I went here. I saw this thing do this action. I picked up the edan." Okay, the first two examples I made up, but the third certainly happens. All the prose reads this way. There's no punch to it, and frankly, I was a little bored. <br /><br />This is not touching on the fact that what themes there are about acceptance and overcoming differences just aren't incorporated well. This is advertised as a Science Fiction novella, but it reads like middle-grade or the lower spectrum of Young Adult. The ending of this entry was far too neat and tidy, especially considering the atrocities committed by certain characters in the story that are quite literally hand-waved away by Binti's intervention and a heartwarming speech. <br /><br />Like I said, I expected more - but it was okay. Unfortunately I don't think this generated enough interest for me to continue. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18073652204810763518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2388775057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2388775057" />
    <a title="Jean Menzies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6206860-jean-menzies"><img alt="Jean Menzies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358274654p2/6206860.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2388775057?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean Menzies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean Menzies" href="/user/show/6206860-jean-menzies">Jean Menzies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765385253" href="/book/show/25819514-binti">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6206860-jean-menzies?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6206860-jean-menzies?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6206860-jean-menzies?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2388775057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6230037359012262378">Review originally published on my blog: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://morejeansthoughts.wordpress.com/2018/05/27/binti-by-nnedi-okorafor/'>https://morejeansthoughts.wordpress.c...</a><br/><br/>This book blew me away with the emotional impact it was able to have in less than one hundred pages. A novella as opposed to a full-length novel this book is the first in a series, of which two more are already available (and I’m half way through number two). It follows our protagonist Binti, a member of the Himba people who are one of multiple cultures that live on Earth. The Himba tend to remain in their own commun</span>
  <span id="freeText6230037359012262378" style="display:none">Review originally published on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://morejeansthoughts.wordpress.com/2018/05/27/binti-by-nnedi-okorafor/">https://morejeansthoughts.wordpress.c...</a><br /><br />This book blew me away with the emotional impact it was able to have in less than one hundred pages. A novella as opposed to a full-length novel this book is the first in a series, of which two more are already available (and I’m half way through number two). It follows our protagonist Binti, a member of the Himba people who are one of multiple cultures that live on Earth. The Himba tend to remain in their own community and never do they leave Earth. Binti, however, is the first of her people to have been offered a place at Oomza University, situated on a planet other than her own, and she is not about to turn it down.<br /><br />This is where our story begins: Binti leaving home silently in the early morning to travel through space and attend Oomza University. The next few pages are packed full of action; nothing unfurls as you may perhaps have expected from the offset of the novella. For a story confined to less than one hundred pages it is impossible to be disappointed by the sheer degree of content, character exploration and sci-fi goodness. The length does, however, restrict the author’s ability to provide detailed world building behind the science in this futuristic setting and how far perhaps the universe has come since today.<br /><br />This is one where readers need to be willing to entirely suspend their disbelief and enter into Binti’s world with whole-hearted acceptance. Of course, this is only possible when the author has spent time and energy carefully constructing the world that is there. Although you may not be provided with pages explaining the process of each piece of science or human development contained within the novella’s pages, there is little question that everything fits together seamlessly and has a reason even if there is only a short time to dwell on it.<br /><br />The character of Binti herself is the focus of this story; she provides an anchor for any reader in a world floating around in the unknown. We follow her pursuit of what she wants whilst struggling to let go of what others expect of her. We watch as she attempts to find the balance between her culture and her decision to go against what is the norm for her people. She is a multifaceted character who is able to assert herself as all of these aspects of her personhood and she will not let others dismiss her.<br /><br />Whether you are a die-hard science fiction reader or a newbie to the genre Binti, is to me, one worth checking out. Following Binti’s journey in Binti was emotional and encapsulating and luckily enough for all of us there are two more books in the series where Binti’s story can continue (and both are longer than the first so that’s a bonus). I’ll confess I have already read the sequel Binti: Home, which I loved equally, and will be starting the third and final book Binti: The Night Masquerade ASAP.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6230037359012262378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2423548973" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2423548973" />
    <a title="Beverly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68708752-beverly"><img alt="Beverly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505852430p2/68708752.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2423548973?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverly" href="/user/show/68708752-beverly">Beverly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2423548973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6049624936459170293">Great novela by the author of Who Fears Death, Binti tells the story of a brilliant, brave young girl who risks everything to go to college, including her family, home and even her life.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1535292658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1535292658" />
    <a title="Thomas Wagner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1276273-thomas-wagner"><img alt="Thomas Wagner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551211339p2/1276273.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1535292658?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Wagner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Wagner" href="/user/show/1276273-thomas-wagner">Thomas Wagner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1535292658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1005370857724728948">Those of you who know me know how ridiculously hard it is to get a 5-star rating out of me. But this is master-class SF storytelling. Some novellas you read and think, "I wish this had been a novel." Some you read and think, "It's a bloated short story." <i>Binti</i> is quite possibly as close to perfect as it could have been, at its exact length. Full-length review coming.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2813648606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8768396119623506416">I didn't really enjoy this. It seemed a bit all over the place and the amount of times the word <i>otjize</i> was said in every section really bothered me by making it repetitive. There was a part of the story where the main character talks about having equations going through her mind to be able to make a complex and satisfying choice like something no one has ever done before... and then the author puts a^+b^=c^. Pythagoras. Something you learn in year6 when you're 11. She's meant to be a genius math</span>
  <span id="freeText8768396119623506416" style="display:none">I didn't really enjoy this. It seemed a bit all over the place and the amount of times the word <i>otjize</i> was said in every section really bothered me by making it repetitive. There was a part of the story where the main character talks about having equations going through her mind to be able to make a complex and satisfying choice like something no one has ever done before... and then the author puts a^+b^=c^. Pythagoras. Something you learn in year6 when you're 11. She's meant to be a genius mathematician! Overall, fairly disappointing and I will not be carrying on with the series.<br /><br />2 disappointing stars.</span>

<div id="review_3437023920" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3437023920" />
    <a title="Ashleigh (a frolic through fiction)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16276747-ashleigh-a-frolic-through-fiction"><img alt="Ashleigh (a frolic through fiction)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600437893p2/16276747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3437023920?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashleigh (a frolic through fiction)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashleigh (a frolic through fiction)" href="/user/show/16276747-ashleigh-a-frolic-through-fiction">Ashleigh (a frolic through fiction)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3437023920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8513993622105593935">I quite enjoyed this one! I really appreciated Binti as the main character - seeing her academic ambition combined with the wavering questioning about going against the norm was something I wholeheartedly got behind pretty much immediately. I was rooting for her through the story as she tried navigating spaces completely new to her, and yet used her intuition to make the best of it. Add in the plot line of a possible war over stolen heritage, and you have yourself a fab scifi novella here! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TI5FB6FOR74jyyo3faUhvoGrbkwWIJRMx/vcyk2em6afl5tis2sXSzAHfe/Pey+Q+wWAUlka+Pi/0Ff1CpoIew==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('J6z4Gb2JTBk66VsjecdJz58Q9B3MgKzVvVNG/nLFJ8f0tSZ8r6wc7CklDPvLGUfh5b4aA4O6wGHFeM3BNcG0Gg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1920299394268429273">Nnedi Okorafor is a Nigerian-American author of African-based science fiction and fantasy (Africanfuturism and Africanjujuism). Okorafor has won a Hugo, a Nebula, a World Fantasy Award, and a Locus Award, and her many fans include Neil Gaiman, Rick Riordan, John Green, and Ursula Le Guin. She is writing a series for Marvel about Shuri, Black Panther’s sister, and has a number of book-based project</span>
  <span id="freeText1920299394268429273" style="display:none">Nnedi Okorafor is a Nigerian-American author of African-based science fiction and fantasy (Africanfuturism and Africanjujuism). Okorafor has won a Hugo, a Nebula, a World Fantasy Award, and a Locus Award, and her many fans include Neil Gaiman, Rick Riordan, John Green, and Ursula Le Guin. She is writing a series for Marvel about Shuri, Black Panther’s sister, and has a number of book-based projects in development for film and TV – including HBO’s adaptation of her novel Who Fears Death, with George R. R. Martin signed on as executive producer. Okorafor is also co-writing the screenplay of an adaptation of Octavia Butler’s Wild Seed with filmmaker Wanuri Kahiu for Amazon Prime Video, with Viola Davis producing. Her novel Akata Warrior (of the Akata Series) is the winner of the Lodestar and Locus Award for Best Young Adult Novel. </span>
